### [4.44b] ITALIAN ORGANIZATION AT ARRIVAL CHART

This chart divides the Italian units into groupings termed "sheets." For example, the 16th "Pistoia" Division sheet lists all of the counters used in CNA to represent the forces historically assigned to the 16th Semi-motorized Infantry Division.

The following sheets represent something of a compromise between game and simulation. There were a great many unassigned and ad hoc Italian units; certainly the number of artillery units — as compared to the opposition, and even those of the Germans — is almost staggering. Likewise, many of these units were captured in entirety or completely destroyed. Records for these units are scarce and somewhat

contradictory. We have attempted to provide every unit we could get accurate research on, on a battalion-regiment level. To that end many units have been “melted” into others, for the sake of simplicity and, to be honest, the parameters of the counter-mix. For example, all the Italian 81mm mortar companies have been abstracted into other artillery units or headquarters units’ values.

Each nation's Order of Battle had its own peculiar difficulties; the Italian's was confusion and profusion. Of the three OB's for the game, it is probably the least accurate historically. This group includes all of the units colored and specified on the counter sheet as Italians.

Formation: The grouping of units in this sheet, Basic Morale: The rating for all of the units listed on this sheet. Unit Assignment: This is indicated by the position of a unit't name in the "Unit" column. A unit whose name is not indented does not possess a parent formation. A unit whose name is indented two spaces possesses a parent formation. Its parent unit is the first unit above it on the sheet whose name is not indented. A unit whose name is indented four spaces possesses two parent units. The brigade-equivalent parent unit is the first unit above it whose name is indented two spaces. Its division-equivalent parent unit is the division headquarters counter. Certain abbreviations of unit names have been made. Those that are not explained in: the Notes are as follows: SIZE-DESIGNATION (actual name, not its size equivalent): Div = Division; Regt = Regiment; Bn = Battalion; Coy or Koy = Company; Bty = Battery. (Note these are the English translations.) TYPE: HQE = Headquarters with engineering capability; HQ = Headquarters without engineering capability; Arty = Artillery; AT = Anti-tank; AA =

Anti-air; Inf = Infantry; MG = Machinegun; Mtr = Motorized; Mitrg = Motorcycle; Heavy Wpns = Heavy Weapons; SchwInf (Schwertze-Infanteriegeschutzten) = Heavy Weapons. OTHER: CCNN = The abbreviation for Camicie Nera (which is Italian for 'Blackshirt'); RECo = Raggruppamento Esplorante Companie (reconnaissance company)' Gaf S di C = Guardia alla Fronteria, Settore di Coperature (roughly translates as Garrison Troops), These GaF units were made up. Europeans living in Libya "dragooned" for the occasion. They were poor troops at best; CD = Coastal Defense. Counter Abbr.: The type as it appears on the counter's unit identification line.ID Code: Indicates the unit's basic characteristics thru the use of a letter key. The explanation of these characteristics is listed in the Italian Unit Characteristics Chart. TOE & Weapon System(s): Indicates the number and type of TOE Strength Points the unit possesses upon its arrival/deployment. The following are used for non-tank or -gun units: N = The unit possesses the maximum number of TOE

Strength Points listed on the Unit Characteristics Chart for that ID Code. U@ = Understrength at 'x' TOE Strength Points. The unit arrives/deploys with that number of TOE Strength Points. O @ = Overstrength at 'x' TOE Strength Points. The unit arrives/deploys with that number of TOE Strength Points, but may only absorb replacement points up to the maximum number permitted for that ID Code. Tank and gun TOE Strength Points (even if assigned to a non-tank or -gun unit) are always listed by number of each Weapons System. For example: A unit possessing six 65/17 Gun TOE Strength Points and four 75/18 Gun-Howitzer TOE Strength Points would be listed as: 6 65/17 Gun & 4 75/18 Gun-Howitzer. It is not indicated whether the TOE Strength Points exceed or are less than the maximum number permitted for that type of unit. Arrives: The date, in CNA game terms, on which the unit is placed on the game map. D = Deployed. The unit begins the first Operations Stage of Game Turn One on the game map. #/- = The Operation /Stage of the Game Turn the unit arrives. -/# = The Game-Turn on which the unit arrives.

Notes:

a = The Ariete Division, probably the best Italian division in the desert, had a variety of different OB's during the campaign. For example, it was reinforced by units stripped from the Littorio upon the latter's arrival. The above OB and TOE covers the initial arrival of the Ariete's units (it went into battle in April, 1941 with a somewhat different OB).

b = This was originally the 32nd R.C.

c = A conglomeration of the 72nd, 132nd, and 142nd Anti-tank Companies.

d = The regiment took on several 75/18 self-propelled Sermovente's stripped from the Littorio.

e = The two Light Tank battalions are attached, not assigned. They are listed here as they arrived with the Ariete and saw a considerable amount of combat while controlled by the division.

<!-- page 148 -->

133rd "Littorio" Divisione Corazzata (Armored) (a)

| Basic Morale: 0Notes Unit | CounterAbbreviation | IDCode | TOE & Weapon System(s) | Arrives |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Littorio (133rd) Div HQE | Littorio | d | 1 × L6/40 | 3/62 |
| 133rd Regt Corazzata HQ | 133 RC | d | 1 × L6/40 | 3/62 |
| X(M) Tank Bn | X(M) | l | 5 × M13/40, 2 × M14/41 | 3/62 |
| X(I) Tank Bn | XI(M) | l | 7XM14/41 | 3/62 |
| XII(M) Tank Bn | XII(M) | l | 4 × M13/40, 3 × M14/41 | 3/62 |
| 12th Bersaglieri Regt HQ | 12 Brs | c | N | 3/62 |
| 23rd Bersaglieri Mtr Bn | 23/12 Brs | t | N | 3/62 |
| 36th Bersaglieri Mtr Bn | 36/12 Brs | t | N | 3/62 |
| RECo ‘Lanceria di Novara’ | LancNov | vv | N | 3/62 |
| 3rd Articelere Regt |  |  |  |  |
| 21st Artillery Bn | 21/3 | kk | 3 × 100/17 Howitzer, 6 × Light AA | 3/62 |
| V Articelere Bn | V/3 | mm | 2 × Semovente 75/18 SP Gun | 3/62 |
| VI Articleleer Bn | VI/3 | mm | 2 × Semovente 75/18 SP Gun | 3/62 |

Notes:

Notes: a = The 133rd was originally the 33rd (R.C.). Upon its arrival, the Littorio was used almost exclusively as replacements for the exhausted Ariete division, most of its tank and both its self-propelled artillery battalions were stripped. Only upon the later arrival of additional Medium Tank battalions and other articelere battalions did the Littorio actually enter the fighting.

b = The 12th Bersaglieri also had a mitraglieri battalion, the 21st. However, it was sunk in transit and is not included.

c = The original unit was the 133rd Artillery Regiment. However, the inclusion of the two battalions of self-propelled guns made the unit what was called, with more hope than performance, 'Articelere' or 'Fast' artillery. The regimental counter for this unit does not exist.

d = These two battalions contained some of the first Semovente 75/18 self-propelled guns, which proved to be one of the best weapons the Italians possessed. The Vth and VIth were stripped and assigned immediately to the Ariete, and were replaced (later) by the DLV and DLV1 Articelere Battalions.

e = Do not confuse with the 21st Artillery Battalion of the 3rd Artillery Regiment (21/3) unit of the Littorio Division.

|  | Tobruk Light AA Bn | TbrkLt | ss | 8×‘I’ Light AA | D |
| C | The San Giorgio | San Giorgio |  |  |  |

### Notes:

a = There is no headquarters for these artillery regiments as this would permit greater flexibility than actually occurred during the campaign. The three artillery units are not part of the 31st Gaf S di C Infantry Regiment.

b = The five artillery and one anti-aircraft units of the Tobruk Coastal Defense Artillery possess the following characteristics. (1) All of the artillery TOE Strength Points are emplaced and may never be moved. (2) All of the artillery TOE Strength Points may fire at Commonwealth warships (they are considered to be “forward”). The numbers in parentheses for the 2nd, 4th, and 5th CD Artillery Groups indicate the number of TOE Strength Points of the emplaced guns that may barrage land targets. (3) No artillery TOE Strength Points may participate in assault nor may any be destroyed as a result of assault. (4) No artillery TOE Strength

Points may be added to these units. (5) All of the artillery and anti-air TOE Strength Points initially listed for the units have a Capability Point Allowance of zero Capability Points. They possess a CPA of 10 for combat purposes during an Operations Stage. No more than one anti-air TOE Strength Point may be added to any one of the six units during any Operations Stage. (6) The anti-air TOE Strength Points initially listed for the six units are not emplaced and may be motorized by truck points.

c = The San Giorgio was an old Italian cruiser that was partially sunk in Tobruk harbor. It partially blocks the harbor, but may freely fire at Commonwealth warships (it is “forward”) and airplanes using its barrage and anti-air ratings respectively. It may not barrage land targets nor may it ever be attacked by land units. It may not be refloated, although it may be destroyed.

4 No artillery TOE Strength Points may be added to the unit. Only one anti-air TOE Strength Point may be added during any Operations Stage.

5 The artillery TOE Strength Points possess a Capability Point Allowance of zero. They possess a CPA of 10 for combat purposes during an Operations Stage.

described this as the worst regular division in the Italian army.

e = Element of the 152nd “Piceno” Division.

c,d,e = These were units from divisions that Mussolini promised to send to North Africa but never got around to doing so. Some of the divisions went to Greece or Corsica; the above battalions being all that arrived in Africa.

### Italian Battle Groups

### Notes:

Although they did not form battle or combat groups as often as their German counterparts, the practice was not unknown to the Italian Army in Africa. The Armored Division (the Babini Group), the fledgling 3rd Libyan Division (the Maletti Group), and the ragtag formation of quasi-paratroopers known as Group Tonini

are perfect examples. The following is a list of Italian Groups, named after commanders, that may be formed. These are considered to be brigade-level headquarters and can be infantry, armor, infantry-armor, or artillery. Their possible compositions are listed on the Maximum Attachments Chart. There are no counters provided for these groups (Occam's Razor cuts deep in counter-land). Italian Battle Groups: Allegri; Bignami; Calpani; Crucilla; Fabrizi; Ferrara; Moech; Pacquali; and Piana.

Note that it is a single formation and is not composed of a headquarters and maneuver battalion counters.

d = Arrives attached to the 25th Infantry Division.

e = Arrives attached to the 27th Infantry Division.

b&c = During their initial attachment the regiments may acquire two and one infantry battalions respectively, regardless of whether or not this causes the parent division to exceed its formation organization and/or maximum attachment limits.

<!-- page 162 -->

### [4.45c] GERMAN ORGANIZATION AT ARRIVAL CHART

This chart divides the German units into groupings termed “sheets.” For example, the Sonderverband 288 Regiment sheet lists all of the counters used in CNA to represent the forces historically assigned to the Sonderverband 288 Kampfgruppe. This chart includes all of the units colored and specified on the counter sheet as Germans.

The following German terms appear in the OA Chart.

Panzer = Armor; Machinegewehr = Machinegun; Panzerjaeger = Anti-tank; Flak = Anti-air; Aufklarungs = Reconnaissance; Pioneer = Engineer; Schutzen = Motorized Infantry; Kradschutzen = Motorcycle infantry; Gebergs = Mountain infantry; PnzrGrndr (Panzer Grenadier) = “Armored” infantry; SchwInf = Schwertze-Infanteriegeschützen (Heavy Weapons).

### 5th Light (“Leichte”) Panzer Division (Later the 21st Panzer Division)

Basic Morale: +2

|  | II/5 Panzer Bn | II/5 | f | 5 × PzII, 6 × PzIIIH, 2 × PzIVD,1 × PzIVE | 2/22 |
| c | 2nd Machinegewehr Bn | 2 | n | N | 2/24 |

### Notes:

a = In the second Operations Stage of the November IV, 1941 Game-Turn (2/58), the 5th Light Panzer Division was reorganized as the 21st Panzer Division. The counter is replaced by the 21st Panzer's HQ counter.

b = Note that this unit possesses a slightly different organization from that of the 5th Light. The headquarters possess the same (if any) tank TOE Strength Point attached to the 5th Light. Upon its reorganization, the 104th Infantry Regiment (from the 15th Panzer Division) and 155th Artillery Regiment were assigned to the 21st.

c = The units were reassigned to other organizations several times. For example, one or both served with the 200th Panzergrenadier Regiment and the 104th Infantry Regiment at various times during the campaign.

d = The I/75 Artillery Battalion became the II/155 Artillery Battalion of the 155th Artillery Regiment upon the latter's assignment to the division in November of 1941. The Axis Player is provided with both counters but may only replace one with the other (i.e., he may not create a II/155 from replacement points).

| b | 15th Schutzen Bde HQ | 15 | b | N | 1/28 |

|  | 33rd Pioneer Bn | 33 | gg | N | 1/28 |

### Notes:

a = The unit was shifted about a lot. It showed up with the 5th Light and later the (same, but renamed) 21st Panzer.

b = This was the headquarters unit for the 104th and 115th Infantry Regiments. The 15th may be used as an intermediate headquarters unit, in which case it may never possess more than six infantry-type battalions among its attached regiments. The 15th may also be simply used as a conventional regimental (2-Stacking Point) headquarters, in which case it may never possess more than three infantry-type battalions.

c = The 104th became part of the 21st Panzer Division, after the latter's reorganization from the 5th Light late in 1941. At the time of its assignment it was enlarged to contain three battalions. The 104th acted, in many instances, like a Kampfgruppe, attaching several different units at different times.

The 15th Panzer Division is by far the most powerful unit in the game. Adequately supplied and used with skill it is virtually unstoppable. It reflects the marvelous use the Germans made of the divisional organization. It is a lesson in combined arms operations.

<!-- page 165 -->

### Kampfgruppen HQ's (a)

### Basic Morale: That of the attached units

### ID Code: b

### Notes:

a = Kampfgruppen were ad hoc formations (brigade-level) of virtually every type and combination of units. They were formed for specific missions, and reflected the incredible German administrative/organizational flexibility. German units rarely stayed in division formation in Africa, and the use of Kampfgruppen was prevalent. The Kampfgruppen headquarters listed below are a random selection of actual groups formed during the campaign: Gruppe Badde, Gruppe Bach (Bach), Gruppe Dedeking, Kampfgruppe Fischer, Kampfgruppe Graf (Graf), Kampfgruppe Kaiser, Kampfgruppe Knabe (Knabe), Kampfgruppe Kost, Gruppe Marcks (Marks), Kampfgruppe Menny, Kampfgruppe Mitte, Kampfgruppe Pfeiffer (Pfeiffer), Gruppe Schwerin (Schwrn), and Gruppe Voss. These units may be formed and disbanded at will, within the restrictions listed below. If the Axis Player wishes to form more Kampfgruppen that he has battlegroup counters, he may do so.

\1. A Kampfgruppe is formed simply by attaching a German unit to it, thereby creating the unit.

\2. The Kampfgruppe counter must be removed (disbanded) when detaching the final German unit (elimination through combat does not apply). In such a situation any remaining Italian units must be detached and any remaining anti-tank TOE Strength Points assigned to the headquarters become replacement points.

\3. The German Player may never attach/assign more than two artillery-type units to a Kampfgruppe unless it is either the 1st or 2nd Afrika Artillery Regiment headquarters (see the German non-Divisional artillery units sheet).

\4. No more than a total of three Italian units may be attached to all of the German Kampfgruppen in play at any time.

It may contain a maximum of five artillery units at any one time. The units listed under it above were at one point assigned to ArKo 104 (then again, so were many others, including some Italian artillery units!).

c = This is simply its name. The artillery was neither emplaced nor was it required to be of true coastal defense ability/quality/performance.

d = Formerly the 864th Heavy Artillery Battalion.

e = The 1/75 Artillery Battalion of the 5/21 Panzer Division is "reassigned" to the 155th Artillery Regt as its second battalion if the 155th Artillery Regt becomes assigned to the 5/21 Panzer (which occurred in November of 1941). Upon reassignment the 1/75 counter is removed from play and is replaced by the II/155.

f = Formerly the 911th Heavy Artillery Battalion.

*The counter abbreviation "1/772" is incorrect.

Key: CPA = Capability Point Alowance. AA = Anti-air rating. Barrage = Barrage Rating. Anti-armor = Anti-armor rating. Vulnerability = Vulnerability Rating. Armor Protection = Armor Protection Rating. Close Assault Off/Def = The respective Offensive and Defensive Close Assault Ratings. Maximum TOE = The maximum number of TOE Strength Points that the unit may contain. Note that this may be exceeded only due to the unit's arrival/deployment TOE Strength. -- = Not applicable (e.g., an infantry unit has no Vulnerability and may therefore not be harmed by anti-armor fire.) (= May not use that rating if there are any units in that hex that possess Armor and non-parenthesized numbers for that rating. Note that Replacement Points do not prevent the unit from using this Rating. * = The unit retains this Capability Point Allowance regardless of the CPA of the TOE Strength Points assigned. ** = If the unit is comprised entirely of US tank TOE Strength Points, its maximum TOE Strength is nine points. See Commonwealth Tank and Gun Characteristics Chart (Case 4.47) for a list of US tank

TOE Strength Points. + = The unit was historically supplied with enough trucks to entirely motorize its components. Note that only commonwealth battalion and company-equivalent units may be motorized. If motorized, only the unit's Capability Point Allowance changes during the period of its motorization.

Notes: 1) Beginning with the 1/39 Game-Turn, certain Reconnaissance units may be upgraded (see CAse 20.5). 2) Beginning with the 1/75 Game-Turn, infantry battalions with ID Codes of 'k' thru 't' inclusive may be augmented by anti-tank TOE Strength Points (see Case 19.9). 3) Beginning with the 1/87 Game-Turn, infantry battalions with ID Codes of 'n', 'p', 'r' and 's' may be upgraded (see Case 20.77). 4) The two units with ID Codes 'h' and 'j' are non-motorized (although they may be motorized by assigning Truck Points and the SAS may be motorized by a Commonwealth LDG, Case 27.88), regardless of all references in the game-rules to leg infantry giving only CPA's of 8 & 10.

<!-- page 174 -->

### 19.32 ITALIAN FORMATION ORGANIZATION CHART

Unit-Type Composition

(5) xx (2) xx (2) xx 1 xx 1 xx 1 xx = Armored division.

(5) xx (3) III (3) III = Tank Group. In CNA, specifically the Libyan Tank (Game-Turn 1...26) Command.

(5) xx (2) xx (2) xx (2) xx-1 1 xx-1 xx-1 1 xx-1 1 xx-1 1 xx-1= Motorized infantry division.

(5) xx (2) xx (2) xx-1 xx-1 1 xx-1 1 xx-1 1 xx-1= Semi-motorized infantry division.

(5) xx (5) xx-1 (2) xx-1 (2) xx-1 0 xx-1 1 xx-1= Libyan infantry and parachute infantry divisions. Note that the Gruppo Maletti may assign a third regiment.

Number = Total number of replacements points of that type that may be brought in. An item possessing two Numbers may have replacement points equal to the sum of the two numbers brought in. However, the Axis Player is limited to bringing in no more than the first Number during the time period listed. Example: The Axis Player may bring in up to 60 Light AA Replacement Points during the game. However, he may only bring in up to 15 of those points during Game-Turns 4 thru 26. Infantry Replacement Points are further subdivided as- to the rate at which the maximum of 100 infantry replacement points may be planned during game-turns 5 through 24. Max = The maximum number of replacement points of that type that may be planned/brought in per game-turn during the time period listed (however, see f below). Dates: The first game-turn on which the item may be planned (and therefore arrives two game-turns later). 2...24, etc. = The first...last game-turns during which the item may be planned at its listed Max.*All are Autobelinda 41's (ID Code 'vv'). †The maximum number of points that may be planned/brought in per month (Note: by months, not four week cycles from the original week of availability). ‡These points are located in the Tunis box. They are available on Game-Turn 39, there being no two weeks delay. They may be moved by land and/or Axis Coastal Shipping. They do not require any supplies until they reach Map Section "A" proper (i.e., the hexfield). Note that only two points of each type may be "called up" during a game-turn. Note that there are no M 13/39 tank replacements.

| Convoy Route |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | 6 | Bomb Pts |
| Cxx01 | Dxx01 | Dxx01 | Exx01 | Exx11 | Dxx11 | 21... 40 |
| Bxx16 | Cxx16 | Cxx21 | Dxx21 | Exx01 | Dxx01 | 41... 80 |
| Bxx01 | Cxx01 | Cxx11 | Dxx11 | Dxx21 | Cxx21 | 81...120 |
| Axx18 | Bxx16 | Cxx01 | Dxx01 | Dxx11 | Cxx11 | 121...160 |
| - | Bxx01 | Bxx26 | Cxx21 | Dxx01 | Cxx01 | 161...200 |
| - | Axx18 | Bxx20 | Cxx11 | Cxx21 | Bxx26 | 201...260 |
| - | - | Bxx10 | Cxx01 | Cxx11 | Bxx20 | 261...320 |
| - | - | Bxx01 | Bxx26 | Cxx01 | Bxx10 | 321...390 |
| - | - | Axx18 | Bxx20 | Bxx26 | Bxx01 | 391...470 |
| - | - | - | Bxx10 | Bxx20 | Axx18 | 471+ |

Bomb Pts=The column on the Air Bombardment and Secondary Barrage Targets CRT on which the attack is to be resolved. Cxx01 (e.g.) = The location of the qualifying division. The capital letter indicates the Game Map-Section, the two small X's indicate that any north-south hex may be used. The numbers indicate the east-west hexrow which must be used. To determine how many Bomb Points may be used to bomb a specific Axis Convoy, find the number of the Convoy Route along which the naval convoy is being shipped. Read down the column beneath the Convoy Route number until you locate the westernmost hexrow beyond which a qualifying Allied division is situated. (A qualifying Allied division is any complete (i.e., non-shell) Allied division that is east of, or in the same east-west hexrow as, at least one other Allied non-shell division.) Attacks on one Convoy have no effect on the attack strength directed against and/or results against shipping in other convoys.

The planes available are calculated reading the number as a percentage of each type of the planes based on Italy/Sicily, rounding fractions down (e.g., 200 = 200%, or double the number of each type of plane in play). Note that the strategic forces are calculated from all planes on Italy/Sicily, may be used regardless of the number of Axis planes in play actually used and may only be used for that Game-Turn's strategic missions over Malta.
